    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I had a similar question before reading this novel and the answer is: Yes, it is. It isn't about the same characters but it's about a girl who works w<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I had a similar question before reading this novel and the answer is: Yes, it is. It isn't about the same characters but it's about a girl who works with Anna. Anna and Etienne appear a lot in the novel as Lola's friends. Also, if you want to know what happened to them after Anna and the French Kiss, you should definitely read this. Hope i helped. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_217903625" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/217903625" />
    <a title="Sophia." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6520961-sophia"><img alt="Sophia." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1322479535p2/6520961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/217903625?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia." href="/user/show/6520961-sophia">Sophia.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=epic-fail">epic-fail</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=no-plot-is-that-normal">no-plot-is-that-normal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=was-the-author-high">was-the-author-high</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=ridiculous-guy">ridiculous-guy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=can-i-kill-the-hero">can-i-kill-the-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=overrated-as-fuck">overrated-as-fuck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=its-not-okay">its-not-okay</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=really-disturbing">really-disturbing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=professional-help-needed-please">professional-help-needed-please</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=sick-and-twisted">sick-and-twisted</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer217903625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13355875236420651883">Oh, gosh. I really cannot understand all the good reviews for this book (even if half of them were given BEFORE the book actually came out, which, if you ask me, is completely stupid). To say it's overrated is an understatement. <br/><br/>This book is such a huge disappointment. I guess this is a typical example of what happens when you fantasize so much about something that you've actually built up this ideal in your mind... which has nothing to do with reality, sadly. Careful people, <b>spoilers ahead</b>.<br/><br/>I'd </span>
  <span id="freeText13355875236420651883" style="display:none">Oh, gosh. I really cannot understand all the good reviews for this book (even if half of them were given BEFORE the book actually came out, which, if you ask me, is completely stupid). To say it's overrated is an understatement. <br><br>This book is such a huge disappointment. I guess this is a typical example of what happens when you fantasize so much about something that you've actually built up this ideal in your mind... which has nothing to do with reality, sadly. Careful people, <b>spoilers ahead</b>.<br><br>I'd like to begin by saying that I am a big fan of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss__Anna_and_the_French_Kiss___1_" title="Anna and the French Kiss (Anna and the French Kiss, #1) by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna and the French Kiss</a>. That book's a master piece, clearly. I absolutely loved Stephanie Perkins' writing and I couldn't wait to read the companion book. <br><br>But unfortunately, Lola and the Boy Next Door feels like.. I don't know, the biggest letdown of the year?<br><br>First off, I have to say it; Lola surely is the most unbelievable and unlikable narrator, I have ever had the misfortune to read about. I'm sorry. I really wanted to like her, I did. But I hated her. I'm just one year older than she is, but all along the book, I felt like she was twelve. Her reactions, her constant lies, her attitude, everything bothered me... her dress code on top.<br><br>Okay. So I understand the concept of wanting to be different, as well as being into fashion. But this just felt <b>ridiculous and weird and wrong</b>. Seriously, big fake sparkly eyelashes and prom dresses and WIGS every day ? <u>What is wrong with that girl?</u> And how is this supposed to make her relatable? <br>She's self-centered and instead of making her look original, that just showed bad taste and immaturity. At some point she goes to school wearing a dress made out of a sheet and some Cleopatrian make up, hum, hello, ARE YOU FOR REAL?! <br>I understand if you're like eight or if it's Halloween or whatever but being a junior and all? <br><br>How come her parents don't say anything? Aren't they supposed to have a say in their kid's image or something? Don't they ever wonder why she feels the necessity of hiding herself? Of wearing outfits that make her absolutely unrecognizable in the streets? Don't they <i>ever</i> think it might be more than teenage drama? What kind of parents wouldn't sit the kid down and try to figure out what's going on?<br><br>I kept thinking that Lola was disturbed <s>and needed some serious therapy</s> and I knew from the very first scenes I wouldn't like her. She made this HUGE deal out of what happened with the Bells two years ago, nearly passing out when she learns they've come back, breaking plates and all, and when you discover what the whole drama is about, it's pathetic. <b>It was nothing</b>. Over-reacting is her middle name, I swear.<br><br>Which naturally brings me to talk about the main hero of the story, Cricket. <b>I feel so, so sorry that no one in the whole editing world could convince Perkins to change that name</b>. It was just so irritating, it bugged (no pun intended) me the whole time and because of that, I was never, ever able to visualize him as a potential hottie. <br> <br>Imagine you're at the hospital. After 9 months of long and exhausting pregnancy, you now have your baby boy in your arms, and he's perfect. And the smiling nurse comes to you and say "What will be the name of that <i>sweetheart</i>?" and you say ... <u>CRICKET</u>. <br><br>Perkins worked on that book with a simple goal: make teenage girls swoon over the characters, and over the story. <br><br>But for the love of God, people, just tell me!<br><br>HOW AM I SUPPOSED TO BE SWOONING OVER THAT? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360424i/711333._SX540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><s>Did she lose a bet in a drinking game or something ?</s><br><br>So I'm sorry. I really am. <u>But I just can't</u>. It's beyond what I can accept. (And don't even get me started on the too-short-pants-and-pointy-red-shoes, because it's painfully obvious how Perkins tried to give him a wannabe "edgy"/hipster/rock n' roll attitude = so cool. Not. It's geeky and unattractive.)<br><br>Basically, I think what was really disturbing in that story is the lack of any realistic element whatsoever. Simplicity anyone ? Not here: <br>The names (Dolores <s>Umbridge anyone</s>? Cricket? Calliope? Come on now!), the characters, the personalities, the outfits (Lola's and Cricket's, for that matter), family situations (I hate it when authors try to send a message like this. What was that supposed to mean? That gay parents can raise a kid just as well as any straight parents? As far as I'm concerned I didn't think that Lola was a normal teenager. Any social worker would be seriously concerned to see her wearing her freakin' Marie Antoinette dress...), the whole inventor thing (Do I even need to talk about that?), as well as the <b>moon-talking</b> (honestly? Like you're seventeen, and you sit on your balcony and talk out loud to the moon, all of this when your window is two inches away from your crush's window? Riight). Nothing felt REAL!<br><br>Perkins tried too much to differentiate her characters, just so her book would be nothing like the clichés of the YA lit world. She tried too hard. <u>Way too hard</u>. Everything was overdone. And the thing is, she doesn't even need to try that hard! <br><br>Perkins is an amazing writer; her work can be amazing, where tons of others just fail miserably. She doesn't need to develop extraordinary characters. Anna didn't have anything special but she was adorable.<br><br>Also, the love triangle was very badly achieved. From the first page, I think, Lola describes Max with the words "tattooed, 22 years old, rock star, pot-addicted, hated by the parents"... I mean, hey, diabolizing much ? (And a five year difference isn't SUCH a big deal. No, it just isn't. St Clair's reaction was ridiculous. Seriously, grow the fuck up Lola. If you keep thinking he's too old to the point of screwing up your relationship, then you're definitely too young.) <br><br>You know what, I think that's precisely the problem actually. Lola felt too young. Like Perkins aimed the book at a younger audience. <s>And if you could relate to Lola and to the way she dresses, then you're probably young, too. You'll change your mind in a couple of years.</s> <br><br>And of course, there's the whole "reverse plot" that everyone spotted. Now it's Lola who's in a relationship, and she has sex YOU GUYS so she's MATURE! But the whole detective thing with her best friend and everything.. It really felt like she was still a young teenager, and that's not what I want to read. I personally like it better when the characters of the books I read are a bit older than me (I suppose it makes me expect great adventures for the years to come or something like that).. But here, I felt like I'd borrowed a book from the middle school's library. And when Lola's acting like a stupid toddler.. it just makes me want to close that damn book and move on. <br><br>And the title was also a bad choice. Yes, yes, it's cute and all the 13 year olds will love it but since you know that the title is "boy next door", it was so obviouuus. So Lola virtually spends the whole story with some guy who you just KNOW is the wrong one. The more you read, the more Max is being described as an asshole - in case you didn't know you HAD to hate him and expect <s>the fly</s> Cricket to come and end up with Lola. <br>The whole goal of love triangles is that you ache NOT knowing what choice would be the best.. Here, we're just left waiting for Lola to open her eyes and stop acting like a lying kid. <u>It's exhausting, really</u>.<br><br>There's another problem, which was SO irritating I wanted to throw the book away. Anna and Etienne. Please. PLEASE. I adored them in their OWN book, here they're just this ridiculous idealized version of a perfect couple, and I found myself cringing whenever they were saying cheesy pseudo romantic bullshit. I mean come on. Like, three months ago, Etienne was still with Ellie, doing his Spanish homework and whining like a baby that he didn't want to be alooone. So don't blame me for laughing out loud when he says oh-so-very-seriously "When you know, you know!"<br><br>Which makes me think about this awful scene that I found absolutely <u>revolting</u> :<br><br>So Lola's upset and she wants to talk about it with Anna, but she says reluctantly "I know you're just going to repeat everything to St Clair." <br><br><i>(This is the part where you expect Anna to say "Are you kidding? Of course not. It's not his business. Besides I have my own life, you know. We're not pathetic codependent idiots. What's going on? Talk to me")</i><br><br>Silly me.<br>Anna actually GRINS broadly and says "Yep". <br>(YEP. I swear that's what she answers!) <br><br><b>Seriously ? What kind of friend is that ?</b> So basically, Perkins, being with someone means you can no longer be a friend and keep a secret without telling your <s>fucking</s> soul mate? <br><br>It was really annoying that repeatedly throughout the book, Etienne's mentioned as the-guy-ALWAYS-sticking-around-Anna, I don't think it's healthy not to have certain aspects of your life where you can be apart from each other. Besides, some stuff like the shrugs of Etienne were okay when it was noticed from Anna's point of view, here I think it was too much (<s>and can I mention that I'm French and none of my friends "full-body" shrug that way?!..</s>).<br><br>Overall, I'd say I couldn't bring myself to care about the (very boring) description of San Fransisco ; or the characters, or the plot, or anything, really. Actually I skimmed <s>a lot</s> through the book and while reading other reviews, I realized that I've missed a good part of the actual story. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Like Lola goes through a goth/OMG-Im-so-miserable-I-only-dress-in-black period? HAHAHA <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>It's a shame because I know what Perkins can do and this is why I won't give up on her. I'm sorta curious of her new book. Which I think is about Isla &amp; Josh from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss__Anna_and_the_French_Kiss___1_" title="Anna and the French Kiss (Anna and the French Kiss, #1) by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna and the French Kiss</a>. That does seem cool, Josh has the potential to be really interesting. I also read somewhere it took place in Paris or something so maybe it'll be better than this one. I hope so, anyway. Thanks for reading !</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="13355875236420651883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_143127464" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143127464" />
    <a title="tonya." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4358824-tonya"><img alt="tonya." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350794820p2/4358824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143127464?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="tonya." class="user" itemprop="url" name="tonya." href="/user/show/4358824-tonya">tonya.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4358824-tonya?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4358824-tonya?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4358824-tonya?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4358824-tonya?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4358824-tonya?shelf=favorites-of-2011">favorites-of-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4358824-tonya?shelf=swoons">swoons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4358824-tonya?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4358824-tonya?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143127464" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer926598891085495979">Here's the thing. I think Stephanie Perkins is in my head. Or at least my daydreams. How else could she consistently write characters that seem to be tailor-made to hit my flutter buttons? Etienne for my anglophilia, Max for my tattooed, Buddy Holly glasses wearing <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[messed up, misdirectedly (I know that's not a word) angry, kind of douchebaggy <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> rocker boy, and Cricket. Cricket for everything I've ever wanted in a <i>real</i> boy. <br/><br/>Because that's the beauty of <i>Lola and the Bo</i></span>
  <span id="freeText926598891085495979" style="display:none">Here's the thing. I think Stephanie Perkins is in my head. Or at least my daydreams. How else could she consistently write characters that seem to be tailor-made to hit my flutter buttons? Etienne for my anglophilia, Max for my tattooed, Buddy Holly glasses wearing <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[messed up, misdirectedly (I know that's not a word) angry, kind of douchebaggy <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> rocker boy, and Cricket. Cricket for everything I've ever wanted in a <i>real</i> boy. <br /><br />Because that's the beauty of <i>Lola and the Boy Next Door</i>. It's real. As much as I loved <i>Anna and the French Kiss</i> (and I looooooooooooooooooooove <i>Anna</i>), <i>Lola</i> was better on nearly every level because it felt <i>real</i>. Anna was by no means a fairy tale without the struggle of realism, but there were some elements that took it to daydream level. Paris. Beautiful, charming British boy. The big, dramatic (incredibly swoontastic) ending.<br /><br /><i>Lola</i> is different. They aren't in Paris, and Cricket isn't a dashing, gorgeous Brit. He's just a normal boy. A normal, awkward, amazingly sweet boy who I can't even find words to describe. (Except for, you know, those...) <br /><br />I won't say anything about the story itself, except Stephanie Perkins manages to surprise me with the depth she gives her characters and their circumstances. Lola made me ache; I went through each moment of impulse, confusion, and agonizing indecision with her. I laughed with her, I certainly cried with her more than I expected to, and I swooned so hard that by the last section I was literally reading standing up because I was FEELING TOO MANY FEELINGS to sit. <br /><br /><i>Lola and the Boy Next Door</i> is everything first love should be--painful, awkward, desperate, tender and so, so sweet. <br /><br />And as I read Perkins' acknowledgements at the end, I found myself tearing up again at her note to her husband. I realized why she is able to write such amazingly real and heartfelt love stories. It's because she's lived it.<br /><br /><i>Lola and the Boy Next Door</i> comes out in September. I can't wait to swoon with you! </span>
  <a data-text-id="926598891085495979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_177519189" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177519189" />
    <a title="Flannery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/652877-flannery"><img alt="Flannery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312843258p2/652877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177519189?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Flannery" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Flannery" href="/user/show/652877-flannery">Flannery</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People Who Read Anna &amp; The French Kiss</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=read-on-tour">read-on-tour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=arc-galley-or-first-reads">arc-galley-or-first-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=young-adult-teen">young-adult-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177519189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer215328371020301159"><b>Did you read Anna and the French Kiss?:</b><br/>A.YES, I loved it! <br/>B.YES, it was okay.<br/>C.YES, and I didn’t like it.<br/>D.NO, but I intend to.<br/>E.NO, it’s not for me.<br/><br/>If you picked A, B, or D, please proceed to review #1.<br/>If you picked C or E, please proceed to review #2.<br/>__________________________________________________<br/><u>Review #1:</u><br/>LOVE! This book is fun, fun, fun (til her daddy takes the T-bird away). It has a very similar feeling to its companion novel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss' title='Anna and the French Kiss by Stephanie Perkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Anna and the French Kiss</a>—a teenage girl who already has a boyf</span>
  <span id="freeText215328371020301159" style="display:none"><b>Did you read Anna and the French Kiss?:</b><br />A.YES, I loved it! <br />B.YES, it was okay.<br />C.YES, and I didn’t like it.<br />D.NO, but I intend to.<br />E.NO, it’s not for me.<br /><br />If you picked A, B, or D, please proceed to review #1.<br />If you picked C or E, please proceed to review #2.<br />__________________________________________________<br /><u>Review #1:</u><br />LOVE! This book is fun, fun, fun (til her daddy takes the T-bird away). It has a very similar feeling to its companion novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss" title="Anna and the French Kiss by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna and the French Kiss</a>—a teenage girl who already has a boyfriend falls for a guy who seems practically perfect in every way, except his family doesn’t appreciate him as much as they should. The current boyfriend is sort of a douchebag and plays in a band and the protag is quirky. The main character in this one, Delores (Lola) Nolan, lives with her two dads in San Francisco. (Remember that show ‘My Two Dads’? I totally forgot about it until this moment) She loves fashion and spends a ton of her time designing and sewing costumes and putting together all sorts of crazy outfits. In the first few pages, Lola sees a moving truck and I think it is no spoiler who is moving in NEXT DOOR-- her love interest. (see: title of the book) Cricket Bell is tall, stylish, and always inventing all sorts of things. His family’s been on the move a lot because his sister is a world-class figure skater and her career dominates the family. Lola’s never gotten along with Calliope but she got along fine (*winkwinknudgenudge*) with Cricket before they moved away two years prior. That is, except for the last day she saw him. Now he’s back and it is reconciliation time. There’s only one boyfriend standing in the way.<br /><br />Lola frustrated me a bit because several of her problems are self-inflicted. I know it isn’t always the easy thing to do but if you are dating someone and totally have the hots for someone else, you are a huge d-bag if you don’t break it off. Sure, the other person’s feelings will be hurt but no one likes looking like a fool after the fact. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Max sucks anyway, let’s be honest. Though his name is a hell of a lot better than CRICKET. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I did like Lola as a character but I wish/ed that she would man up, stop leading Cricket on, and be a better friend to Lindsay. <br /><br />Anna and St. Clair make much more of an appearance than I thought they would. They actual show up throughout the entire novel and it was a plus and minus situation for me. I was happy to see characters I knew but I have probably read 100 books since Anna and I no longer remembered the details of their true love always and forever relationship so their constant togetherness was a bit off-putting to me. Like those newish couples who are always PDAing all over the place. <br /><br />I’m a pretty huge sucker for boy next door stories. Or really any situation where someone awesome has been under the protag’s nose for years. I hope I am not making it sound like I hated this book. I was annoyed with Lola quite a bit but I really LOVED most of this book. And you know what made this book even better for me? That my friends sent it to me with their comments written in it. I absolutely adored reading their thoughts and adding my own for people later on the tour list. <br /><br />I really enjoyed this and will keep reading anything Stephanie Perkins writes…but a little more than a little of me wants to see how she handles something other than this storyline. <br /><br />Thank you so, so much Arlene for sharing your copy with me!<br /><br /><u>Review #2:</u><br />You probably won’t like this book. Move along, nothing to see here.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="215328371020301159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_136242049" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136242049" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136242049?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ari by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/5273538-jojo---jjj-jo-anna-janesko">JoJo - JJJ (Jo Anna) Janesko</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=next-door">next-door</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136242049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10922134970812002923"><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/stephanie-perkins/lola-and-the-boy-next-door-review.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342853i/698565.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I'm definitely going to burn in hell..<br/>Oh, that awkward moment when everybody loves a book and you don't understand why... You know that feeling, right? Well, yeah, I'm pretty much living it.<br/><br/>It's not that I DIDN'T LIKE the book, it's just that I didn't LIKE it.. Does it make any sense to you, because for me there is a whole damn big difference.<br/><br/>Anyways, this is not Anna's book-sister, this is more like the evil stepsister.. It  actually managed to  raise my blood pressure, unfortunately not in</span>
  <span id="freeText10922134970812002923" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/stephanie-perkins/lola-and-the-boy-next-door-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342853i/698565.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I'm definitely going to burn in hell..<br>Oh, that awkward moment when everybody loves a book and you don't understand why... You know that feeling, right? Well, yeah, I'm pretty much living it.<br><br>It's not that I DIDN'T LIKE the book, it's just that I didn't LIKE it.. Does it make any sense to you, because for me there is a whole damn big difference.<br><br>Anyways, this is not Anna's book-sister, this is more like the evil stepsister.. It  actually managed to  raise my blood pressure, unfortunately not in a <em>"too hot to handle"</em> kind of way.<br><br>I've generously given this book 2.5 stars because I love Stephanie's style. Not only because I loved <a title="Anna and the French Kiss Review" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/stephanie-perkins/anna-and-the-french-kiss-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna </a>but because I follow Stephanie's  blog and I love her posts, her wittiness, her optimism, her joy of life. She makes me laugh a lot.. But Lola, Lola was just not right for me and I really struggled to understand why did all those people love it so much.<br><br>First I didn't like (whinny) Lola.. Or (dorky) Cricket for a matter of fact. (Yes, I know you all love him but I just can't understand why)<br>Then I liked Max.<br>Did you just have a heart attack? No? Ok then, Because i need you to listen to me.<br><br>I'll start from the beginning...<br><br><em>1. LOLA:</em><br><br>I didn't care about her, her wigs, her pink and glittering room, her past with the twins, and her memories from when she was 5 years old.<br>I found her to be really immature, and she was complaining way too much.<br>She kept denying her feelings for 3/4 of the book and when her best friend (Lindsey) said that it was obvious that she liked Cricket then *bang* the truth hit her.<br><blockquote>"I open my window and a thousand bottled emotions explode inside of me at the full sight of him.<br>I like Cricket. Like that.<br>Again."</blockquote><br>No s**t.. after 200 pages of whining about how he hurt you, and how you don't want to like him, and how you like him but you want to be with your boyfriend (to whom you lie all the time BTW). The realization just hit you one moment... just like that?<br>And I had to hear you all that time complaining and complaining, and playing with Cricket's feelings just.. because...?!<br><br>Let me tell you this:<br>In "<a title="Anna and the French Kiss Review" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/stephanie-perkins/anna-and-the-french-kiss-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna</a>" there was this cute flirting between the main characters and some nice friendship going on.. I understood why Anna liked Etienne, even as confusing as the situation was.<br>In this one I felt sorry for Cricket. He was begging for love from the moment he confessed that he liked her (only a few days after he came back). He was always there for her, like a faithful dog, it broke my heart, really! <br><br>2. CRICKET:<br><br>Talking about Cricket.. He's been described by other reviewers as this sexy geek, swoon worthy that would steal everyone's heart. (no really?!)<br>Did I read the same book?<br><br>*clearing throat*<br><br>Except for his tight pants (yes, apparently he had sexy pants for all I know from Lola's obsessive thinking) there was <em>nothing</em> sexy about him (of course, in my opinion). All Lola's memories of him are awkward and he is described as something totally different and unattractive, and I had a hard time understanding why did she like him in the first place.<br>Because he was the only kid in the world not saying bad things to her? Because he was the boy next door and it's nice to have a crush on your neighbor? I don't know why!<br><br>And then he was mostly absent from this book, coming home only for weekends (not even all of them). Yes she thought about him <em>all the time</em>, from the very beginning, because she was obsessing about him. She said she was unhappy because he came back, but right before that she was whining about losing him. Even in the beginning. She couldn't say something about her boyfriend without remembering the boy next door.<br><br>But it's all his fault.. She had the nerve to say that it was <em>his fault</em> that she was thinking about him.. yeah, blame it all on his return..<br>Do I need to quote her on the first page talking about him when he was not even back yet? No?<br>OK, then I rest my case.<br><br><em>3. PARENTS:</em><br><br>Her family was weird.. I couldn't understand why they were so involved in her life, not agreeing with anything.<br>All she did was wrong, no matter what.<br>You like Max? Wrong!<br>You like Cricket? Wrong! (if he comes to your room)<br>Are you too happy.. Are you sad? Wrong, wrong, wrong!<br><br>I hated the protective fathers... As Max said: one is horrible, 2 unbearable.. I agree!<br>What was that obsession about the age difference?<br>There is something called trust, you know, and you should trust your kids (because if they want to have sex with someone they will do it even with someone their age, there's no need to find someone 5 years older.. Just saying).<br>Still, I liked Alec. He was the 'good father'.  I liked the advices that he gave Lola., how he was there for her, and also I liked that he told her when she was doing something wrong. In a nice way. He was not as absurd as Nathan.<br>As for her mother, she was a mess.<br>With a family like that I don't wonder why is Lola so vulnerable and unsecure and undecided.<br><br><em>4. FRIENDS:</em><br><br>Lindsey was a crappy friend, and there was no trust between them either.<br>In "Anna" I loved the friendship between all those characters, in this one it felt simply unnecessary... Lindsey was there just to crack a joke from time to time, and to boss around telling Lola if she was allowed to like Cricket or not (and to complain about Lola's boyfriend.. what a horrible thing to do - no wonder why Max didn't like her either).  And they were so different that I wondered why in the world were they friends anyways..<br><br>Anna and Etienne were there, but not even they made a good appearance. They were not close friends to Lola, and their relationship with her seemed a bit forced. I hated when Lola let down Anna when she promised to introduce Anna to her boyfriend (Max).<br><br><em>5. BOYFRIEND:</em><br><br><em>Max was the only character in the book that I <strong>liked</strong></em>, but I wasn't suppose too, and he turned out conveniently mean in the end, just to make a point: he was older, he was no good for her, he was not to be trusted, he had to become a jerk, he had to break your heart. DONE! (BTW, when you break up with someone because you like someone else, are you allowed to tell that <em>he</em> broke your heart? I didn't think so!)<br><br>Anyways I felt sorry for him, because I knew that Lola never really liked him, and she was with him only because he was older and she wanted just to show off in front of her friends and to piss her parents.<br>But he was nice, and smart, and he tried a lot to make thing right. He was the only sane character in the book! I was sorry to see him change (personality wise) at the end only to make the situation easier for Lola. What a shame!<br><br>--<br><br>All through this book I kept thinking: how in the world would I understand Lola, if she went against everything I believe in?<br>How could I enjoy her complaining about losing a guy I couldn't care less about (because she made me hate him in the first place), how could I be there for her while lying to her boyfriend (that I actually liked), and so on.<br><br>I understood Etienne in the first book, the story worked in his case... His dad was a big jerk and his mother was dying, and he needed to have something permanent in his life, something to be somehow certain about.. That's why he didn't break up with Ellie, but what is Lola's excuse? Cricket told her what he felt almost in the beginning, and she was toying with his feelings. Remember how some people said that Etienne was playing with Anna's feelings? Well, meet Lola, she is even worse.<br><br>There were some few funny moments, yes, but other than those this book was mostly depressing, with Lola complaining about her love life, and her mother, and Max, and her fathers, and the <em>twins</em>. (oh boy, not the twins again!)<br><br>I still want to read the next book, I can't wait for it, but "Lola and the boy next door" was simply not a book for me.<br>When I read about Christmas in this one, I remembered the Christmas scene from the other one, with the phone calls and messages, oh, it was so damn cute.<br>Even if I didn't like this book as much as I wanted, I can give it credit for making me want to read "<a title="Anna and the French Kiss Review" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/stephanie-perkins/anna-and-the-french-kiss-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna and the french kiss</a>" again, and for making me hope that "<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9627755-isla-and-the-happily-ever-after" rel="nofollow noopener">Isla and the Happily Ever After</a>" will be better.<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/stephanie-perkins/lola-and-the-boy-next-door-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380313075i/688704.jpg" alt="" width="361" height="116" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/stephanie-perkins/lola-and-the-boy-next-door-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a></i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br><br><strong>Favorite quote:</strong><br><blockquote>
  <em>”Because that’s the thing about depression. When I feel it deeply, I don’t want to let it go. It becomes a comfort. I want to cloak myself under its heavy weight and breathe it into my lungs. I want to nurture it, grow it, cultivate it. It’s mine. I want to check out with it, drift asleep wrapped in its arms…”</em>
</blockquote><br><strong>Music of choice:</strong><br><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IpBjJ0dp2mc" rel="nofollow noopener">Plain White T's - Hate (I Really Don't Like You)</a><br><br>PS: sorry, Jo, that I didn't love this book as you did. I'm glad that you liked it better! :)<br><br><strong>Pre-reading thoughts:</strong><br>God, I'm counting the days here.. ♥<br>Update:<br><s>I officially hate every single person in the world that has read &amp; loved this book because I want to read it too!!!</s><br>No, scratch that, I'm kidding.. I am so happy for you :) *sigh*</span>

  <span id="freeText6816945698349693865" style="display:none">finally getting around to writing a review for this because it came up in conversation and i just now realised what never clicked for me.<br /><br />yes, this is a light and fluffy story. i didnt find it problematic like i did with <i>‘anna,’</i> so thats a good thing. but i never connected with the characters and i finally just figured out why. <br /><br />i appreciate authors trying to make their characters quirky. i get it. everyone has something that makes them awkward and weird. quirky characters are opportunities for readers to relate to non-stereotypes. but have you ever read a character that was just tooo quirky? like, to the point where you dont affectionately say <i>‘you weirdo,’</i> but youre constantly like <i>‘what the heck is this person even doing??’</i> i found both lola and cricket to be too quirky - so much so that they didnt seem like real people to me. <br /><br />so while i actually did like the story/plot concept, the execution of characters just wasnt for me. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3 stars</i></b></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/183666777?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183666777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16614488474081540186"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><i>Yay for warm fuzzies</i>. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3095893.Stephanie_Perkins' title='Stephanie Perkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stephanie Perkins</a> has a talent and that talent is for making me happy, allowing me to enjoy the entire reading experience, laugh at times and come away with no deep sense of revelation - just the knowledge that I will have to get my hands on whatever she writes next. Her writing may be light and mostly meaningless but it achieves one of the greatest things a book possibly can: fun.<br/><br/>And that's just it... this book is silly, mindless fun. I'm not sure why some people who e</span>
  <span id="freeText16614488474081540186" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Yay for warm fuzzies</i>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3095893.Stephanie_Perkins" title="Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephanie Perkins</a> has a talent and that talent is for making me happy, allowing me to enjoy the entire reading experience, laugh at times and come away with no deep sense of revelation - just the knowledge that I will have to get my hands on whatever she writes next. Her writing may be light and mostly meaningless but it achieves one of the greatest things a book possibly can: fun.<br><br>And that's just it... this book is silly, mindless fun. I'm not sure why some people who enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss" title="Anna and the French Kiss by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna and the French Kiss</a> didn't like this, for me it was a very similar sort of book in many ways, with the main difference being that I thought Lola was a much more well-rounded and interesting character than Anna. I also liked Cricket a lot more than Etienne St.Clair. Perhaps it's the height thing, or that a lot of Etienne's charm was built around the English accent that I have to hear lecturing me about Plato every day. I thought both were entertaining romance stories but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9961796.Lola_and_the_Boy_Next_Door" title="Lola and the Boy Next Door by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Lola and the Boy Next Door</a> just seemed to suit me better.<br><br>There was only one thing that I didn't like about this book and it was mostly because I thought it unnecessary. It was how the boyfriend who was originally kind, understanding and quirky turned into a complete dick in order to make it alright for Lola to leave him. I think this could have been handled better, sometimes people's feelings change in relationships and you can gently and maturely break it off - did <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3095893.Stephanie_Perkins" title="Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephanie Perkins</a> worry that we'd be unable to forgive Lola for upsetting a good guy so she made him a closet moron instead? It wasn't needed and it didn't flow naturally.<br><br>Apart from that, this was a great book and I can't wait to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9627755.Isla_and_the_Happily_Ever_After" title="Isla and the Happily Ever After by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Isla and the Happily Ever After</a>.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16614488474081540186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_178701598" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178701598" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178701598?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101529485" href="/book/show/11509277-lola-and-the-boy-next-door">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=romancelandia">romancelandia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178701598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12610700784162429036">I don't know how I am going to justify this rating. Books like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9961796.Lola_and_the_Boy_Next_Door' title='Lola and the Boy Next Door by Stephanie Perkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lola and the Boy Next Door</a> rarely work for me. I dislike chick-lit, I dislike two-timing/emotionally cheating/lying heroines, I dislike when the "wrong" guy in books with love triangles is vilified at the last minute to make it right for the heroine to break up with him. And yet I liked this book that contains all these elements. <br/><br/>This novel is just such a light, breezy, charming read. The main character, who would normally annoy the </span>
  <span id="freeText12610700784162429036" style="display:none">I don't know how I am going to justify this rating. Books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9961796.Lola_and_the_Boy_Next_Door" title="Lola and the Boy Next Door by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Lola and the Boy Next Door</a> rarely work for me. I dislike chick-lit, I dislike two-timing/emotionally cheating/lying heroines, I dislike when the "wrong" guy in books with love triangles is vilified at the last minute to make it right for the heroine to break up with him. And yet I liked this book that contains all these elements. <br /><br />This novel is just such a light, breezy, charming read. The main character, who would normally annoy the hell out of me with her obsession with clothes, glitter, tiaras, has a very relatable voice. Reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9961796.Lola_and_the_Boy_Next_Door" title="Lola and the Boy Next Door by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Lola and the Boy Next Door</a> was an infinitely relaxing experience. This book is filled to the brim with cuteness - cute boys, cute families, cute locations and cute crushes. Perkins' special gift is bringing back the memories of young love and excitements and heartaches that come with it. (I would have preferred this book without sex though.)<br /><br />My excuse for liking <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3095893.Stephanie_Perkins" title="Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephanie Perkins</a> debut novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss" title="Anna and the French Kiss by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna and the French Kiss</a> was that I read it around Christmas and it hit just the right spot then. My excuse now will be that I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9961796.Lola_and_the_Boy_Next_Door" title="Lola and the Boy Next Door by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Lola and the Boy Next Door</a> by the pool under the Florida sun in October and it is a perfect beach read. I am running out of the excuses here, so I guess I should just accept the fact that while I have no love for chick-lit, Perkins has a talent to convert even this jaded hater into a fan. There is no doubt, I will be reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9627755.Isla_and_the_Happily_Ever_After" title="Isla and the Happily Ever After by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Isla and the Happily Ever After</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12610700784162429036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_178795327" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178795327" />
    <a title="Limonessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa"><img alt="Limonessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424025988p2/4147373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178795327?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Limonessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Limonessa" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa">Limonessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10787121-lola-and-the-boy-next-door">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=3-neurons-involved">3-neurons-involved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178795327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14706441653638184062">The thing about <i>Lola and the boy next door</i> is that, since it's a companion book, it's inevitable to make a comparison with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss' title='Anna and the French Kiss by Stephanie Perkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Anna and the French Kiss</a> which, in this case, comes out as a disadvantage because, as far as I am concerned, Anna is the absolute winner.<br/><br/><i>Lola</i> is a really cute story: she is a quirky, raised by gay parents, unique teenage girl.<br/>When her first crush and ex-neighbor, Cricket, reappears on her doorstep after two years, things get complicated because Lola already has a boyfriend, </span>
  <span id="freeText14706441653638184062" style="display:none">The thing about <i>Lola and the boy next door</i> is that, since it's a companion book, it's inevitable to make a comparison with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss" title="Anna and the French Kiss by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna and the French Kiss</a> which, in this case, comes out as a disadvantage because, as far as I am concerned, Anna is the absolute winner.<br /><br /><i>Lola</i> is a really cute story: she is a quirky, raised by gay parents, unique teenage girl.<br />When her first crush and ex-neighbor, Cricket, reappears on her doorstep after two years, things get complicated because Lola already has a boyfriend, Max, five years older than her, much more experienced.<br />As Cricket slowly worms his was back into her life - and into her heart - Lola will have to learn how to be honest with herself - and she will learn it the hard way.<br /><br />I'll admit I had high expectations for this book and while it's certainly enjoyable and relaxing, it failed to deliver repeatedly for me.<br />Whereas Anna's story, while still being fluffy, was more believable, less shallow and more charming, Lola's story was definitely more clichéd, more puerile and felt forced in more than one occasion.<br /><br />The most striking example of this "forcedness" is Max.<br />I didn't like how he first gets presented as an awesome boyfriend and then, quite conveniently, ends up being the asshole in a total unreasonable way. It was done unreasonably and felt so contrived, that when he does become an asshole and I was supposed to despise him I just couldn't bring myself to and I still liked him from before!<br /><br />I wonder if it all has to do with the fact that the 5 years of difference in age between Lola and Max are taken as a big NO NO right from the start, because frankly, I didn't buy it. I had a 22 years old boyfriend when I was 17 and it was NOT a big deal. But, since it's taken for granted here that Max is too old for Lola, let's just make him the EVIL guy. The way the author deals with his character royally pissed me off. It wasn't smooth AT ALL.<br />But the same goes for the other characters: basically, they were just <i>too</i> black or white, they lacked depth and originality: Cricket was just too damn good for his own sake, Max too damn bad (kind of in a beautiful and damned way), Lola too damn in self denial: what she says to Max when she goes to his apartment? So not cool, girl. My eye was twitching madly during that passage.<br /><br />Still, it's a book I'd recommend if you're looking for something quite readable and relaxing AND you loved <i>Anna</i>. Perkins certainly knows how to write a story and make her dialogues interesting. It's a colorful book, as colorful as its cover, despite the psycho-looking girl there.<br />I just wish there had been a little more to it, a bit more <i>substance</i>. Anna was definitely more fun for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14706441653638184062" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1652700098" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1652700098?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142422014" href="/book/show/16101168-lola-and-the-boy-next-door">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1652700098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8263870064101989977"><br/>One thing I have to appreciate about this story is its glaring reminder that is to <b>
  <u>NEVER EVER ENTER A SERIOUS RELATIONSHIP WHEN YOU’RE UNSURE OF YOURSELF</u>
</b> and I know age isn’t always an indication of a person’s maturity but in this case and it’s most often, sixteen year olds are yet on their way to discovering who they are and like what I’ve already mentioned, when you’re 16, be 16. I don’t have to explain that further.^^<br/><br/>Truthfully speaking, I didn’t like the significant first half of the sto</span>
  <span id="freeText8263870064101989977" style="display:none"><br />One thing I have to appreciate about this story is its glaring reminder that is to <b>
  <u>NEVER EVER ENTER A SERIOUS RELATIONSHIP WHEN YOU’RE UNSURE OF YOURSELF</u>
</b> and I know age isn’t always an indication of a person’s maturity but in this case and it’s most often, sixteen year olds are yet on their way to discovering who they are and like what I’ve already mentioned, when you’re 16, be 16. I don’t have to explain that further.^^<br /><br />Truthfully speaking, I didn’t like the significant first half of the story AT ALL. I didn’t like Lola’s selfishness and indecisiveness and I hated that because of her uncertainties, she had to string along two perfectly great guys at the same time, thus creating the most terrible love triangle in the history of contemporary YA romance. I also hated this other guy’s character development. Why does he have to be a jerk in the end just to solve the main problem?<br /><br />But just when I was ready to give this a final rating of two stars because I thought there was no possible way to resolve the conflict and give it a decent ending, somehow, the author still managed to do it. It was a relief that at least, Lola realizes all her flaws and fully admits to them and when she started to come to realize her faults, it’s when I started to enjoy the story. I especially liked that when Lola chooses to, she could show all these great qualities about herself like her creativity and cheerfulness. It was also cute to see a glimpse of Anna and Etienne’s relationship.<br /><br />To sum it up, it was generally still a worthwhile, entertaining read and although several parts annoyed the heck out of me, there’s this truthfulness and honesty to the story that I couldn’t help appreciate.<br /><br /><b> P.S. Cricket is love. &lt;3 </b><br /></span>
