  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_194580447" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/194580447" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2753251-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369004887p2/2753251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/194580447?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/2753251-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Die-hard fans of Anna and the French Kiss.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=really-excited-for">really-excited-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=me-and-my-dirty-mouth-review">me-and-my-dirty-mouth-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=highly-anticipated">highly-anticipated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=not-even-okay">not-even-okay</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=surprised-me">surprised-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=ya-romance">ya-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=2011-read">2011-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=i-love-this-cover">i-love-this-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=must-get-asap">must-get-asap</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer194580447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18299926722528557303">You know how all you Harry Potter fans were, like, living for the release of the seventh book, and then how some were disappointed in it? <i>Lola</i> was my disappointing Deathly Hallows. <br/><br/>You see, <i>Anna</i> and I, we hit it off. She smacked me in the face when I needed a slap, she caressed my <s>stupid</s> romantic heart, and she left me laughing out loud and wanting more. <i>Anna</i>, well, she’s kind of the reminder in a genre full of heavy stuff that it’s okay to watch romantic comedies on Valentine’s Day with a box o</span>
  <span id="freeText18299926722528557303" style="display:none">You know how all you Harry Potter fans were, like, living for the release of the seventh book, and then how some were disappointed in it? <i>Lola</i> was my disappointing Deathly Hallows. <br /><br />You see, <i>Anna</i> and I, we hit it off. She smacked me in the face when I needed a slap, she caressed my <s>stupid</s> romantic heart, and she left me laughing out loud and wanting more. <i>Anna</i>, well, she’s kind of the reminder in a genre full of heavy stuff that it’s okay to watch romantic comedies on Valentine’s Day with a box of chocolate and start crying at the end when everyone lives Happily Ever After.<br /><br /><i>Anna</i> reminded us that it’s okay to be gentle and fluffy, and that’s perfectly fine, lalala, I accept and understand that, whatever. <b>But. Once in a while, though</b>. I mean, it’s not like you should watch romantic comedies and cry and eat chocolate on Valentine’s Day EVERY YEAR, because it’s unhealthy and depressing and unfortunate. Just like <i>Lola and the Boy Next Door</i>.<br /><br />Perkins goes for quirky characters in such a way that she’s imitating Dessen’s trademark cast selection and mixing it with Elkeles’ cheesy lines. She also tries to have a little Nicholas Sparks in her books – the Dramatic Stuff – and Meg Cabot – the Funny Stuff. This, all together, creates one. big. mess. because it’s really difficult to include all that stuff and do it well.<br /><br /><b>First Things First: Lola, the Mean Girl Next Door</b><br /><br />Lola was unlikable such a way that I wanted to strangle her from the very first chapter. And, dudes, I happen to <b>like</b> unlikable characters. I ENJOY reading about the bitches and the cruel and the HUMAN people. I mean, Regina (Some Girls Are) and I are <b>tight</b>. I’m fed up with all these nice girls in YA because, HELLO, most people aren’t very nice, no matter how hard they try to be. But Lola was cold and unflattering and (yuck)<i>trying</i> to be likable. Annoyances trying to be sweet and caring and loving just make me go <b>	-_______________- </b><br /><br /><b>(This one scene was supposed to demonstrate how badly Lola treats her best friend Lindsey Lim, but then I realized how it does a really good job of demonstrating how badly Lola treats EVERYONE in general, and of how self-obsessed she is. Pay close attention.)</b><br /><br /><i>‘The plan was to hang out with Max and Lindsey for a few hours and then go home at dusk. […] <b>But now I don’t want to hang out with Lindsey and Max together.</b> And I want to stay with my friend, but I haven’t been alone with Max in two weeks. </i><br /><br /><i>No, I should stay with Lindsey.</i><br /><br /><i>“Max?” she asks.</i><br /><br /><i>“Yeah. He’s ready to meet up, but <b>I’m going to tell him we’re going home early.”</b></i><br /><br /><i>[…] “Yeah, well, you haven’t seen him in forever. <b>Don’t let me stand in the way of your amorous pursuits.”</b></i><br /><br /><i>
  <b>I wish Lindsey would stop talking in front of Cricket.</b>
</i><br /><br /><i>[…]<b>She’s pushing me away out of spite. There’s no good way of dealing with her when she’s like this, except to give her what she wants. “So, um, talk to you tonight?”</b></i><br /><br /><i>“Go,” she says.</i><br /><br /><i>[…]<b>I sneak a look at Cricket before leaving.’</b></i> (Pages 216-217 of <i>Lola and the Boy Next Door</i>)<br /><br />Um, kbro? Everything in bold is what I have a problem with. <br /><br />First, Lola says that she no longer wants to hang out with Lindsey and Max together (they clashed earlier in the book, and Max treated Lindsey like shit). This bothers me because WHAT KIND OF GIRL STICKS WITH A GUY WHO PISSES ON HER BEST FRIEND’S PARADE WHEN SHE’S DONE NOTHING WRONG?<br /><br />Lola, apparently.<br /><br />Next, Lola makes excuses not to see her boyfriend and interrupts the whole evening because of how terribly he gets along with Lindsey. That’s bad, but okay, fine, that could have been dealt with appropriately. Yet, when Lindsey insists that Lola goes with Max because she doesn’t want to be a bad friend, Lola mentally attacks Lindsey’s KIND and FRIENDLY personality in saying “there’s no good way of dealing with her when she’s like this.” Um, she’s like this BECAUSE OF YOU and what you put her through, chicky.<br /><br />Lastly – this is a BIG one – Lola has THE GALL to LOOK AT CRICKET, as if to LOOK APOLOGETIC for leaving, when she should be begging at Lindsey’s feet instead! Excuse me, but Perkins expects us to LIKE Lola and let her cry on shoulders when things don’t go her way?<br /><br />Pssshaw, yeah right.<br /><br />This one scene just demonstrates EVERYTHING WRONG with Lola’s personality. She’s selfish and self-obsessed, she blames other people for her own problems, and she’s a liar. ALSO, throughout the book, Lola progressively treats her best friend – who’s doing absofuckingeverything for Lola that she can to help – like she’s shit off the face of the earth. What sucks overall is that near the end of the book, Lola realizes how terrible a person she is and she even <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[goes into this “huge depression” <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but she NEVER CHANGES. She remains statically horrid.<br /><br />Psshawwww, you think THIS is fun to read?<br /><br /><b>Second Helpings: Dem Supporting Cast, punk</b><br /><br />There’s a pattern bridging, guys. I’ve seen this about ten times in the last year, and I’ve had it UP TO HERE with this trick: authors are demonizing other characters that could be compared with the love interest to make the love interest seem superior. This creates some very unlikable characters, who weren’t meant to be unlikable and who only became unlikable once the love interest is introduced.<br /><br />Perkins creates an older, rocker, bastard of a boyfriend for Lola. In the beginning, he was likable, and if he hadn’t become such an ass over the course of the book – which really isn’t his fault – I <i>still</i> would have preferred him over Cricket as I did originally. What happens is this: as Perkins gives us the chance to get friendly with Cricket, she begins to emphasize how big of an asshole Max is. Over the course of the book, he becomes controlling, mean, and borderline pedophilic-gross…just because Cricket was introduced. And now that I think about it, Perkins did the same thing (albeit, I think she did all this without realizing on both accounts) in <i>Anna in the French Kiss</i> with that kid Dave, who yes had from the start been gross, but had eventually become DISGUSTING just to prove how wunderfuuul St. Clair was. Do you guys smell character fraud, too?<br /><br />And have I mentioned how much I disliked Cricket? He seemed like such a play on the perfect guy “who really isn’t perfect deep down” that I wanted to hurl. God, I love me some eccentric and individual guys, but COME. ON. Cricket was just like Lola in the way that Perkins tried to make him unique, but just ended up mangling his personality in the meantime.<br /><br />And he acted like a puppy dog, seriously. People who can’t stand up for themselves make me wonder sometimes, but those who DEPEND on others’ fondness just annoy me. I sure as hell want people to like me, and yes, it bothers me when they don’t, but I don’t live my life to make other people happy, especially not if they’ll continue to treat me like crap – Cricket, case in point.<br /><br /><b>Third of All: The Elaborate Dresses vs. Writing Style</b><br /><br />I happen to like Stephanie Perkins a lot – she’s funny, she’s pretty darn adorable and she never ceases to inspire me with her blog posts and tweets. <s>In actuality, I hate myself for being so cruel in this review.</s>In <i>Anna and the French Kiss</i> her words touched me and made me want to sob all over my ratty old teddy bear. In her first book, she’d used a lot of clichés (St. Clair is a walking example) and a lot of overused and overtly dramatic phrases, yet it had been fine because that’s just the kind of book <i>Anna</i> was. <i>Lola</i>, though, was not an attempt to be flowery and truwuv-loveydovey in the way that <i>Anna</i> was, even though it certainly had those aspects involved – it was meant to be a book that was about finding yourself and uniqueness and self-realization. What happens is Perkins loses her point EXACTLY the way Lady Gaga has – she’s focused too much on the outer design and the overall gorgeousness of the product instead of tying that to “what’s inside” and “what’s really important.” <br /><br />Lola’s outfits astounded me and all, but they were just so out-there and pointless to the story. I understand where Perkins was trying to go with the whole “designer” thing that Lola did, but that point was lost in all the drama I dealt with above, and also because she never really talked about how largely designing affected Lola, and why she was so dependant on having a unique style. From time to time, Perkins would sit Lola down and have her struggle with her prom dress, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and then, yes, there was the whole Back-in-Black episode <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but it was still really unclear what made Lola choose such an outlet for individuality and why she was so indulgent with it.<br /><br />The writing lacked to prove Lola’s uniqueness, but it also was just a lot of clichés and cheesy phrases and boring romantic encounters. I saw next to no chemistry between Lola and Cricket. Everything that was meant to be funny…wasn’t. All the monumental “self-realizing” scenes were dry. It was like dead flowers were strewn throughout the story – ideas originally beautiful turned to dust.<br /><br /><b>Fourthly: The Plot, a Reboot of <i>Anna</i></b><br /><br />I’m getting tired, aren’t you? I wish I could stop my review right here with a READ IF YOU MUST sign and a little happy face. Jesus, guys, this is longer than my final essay in AP English. Alas, though, I still must talk about the plot.<br /><br />Because, WHAT IS A BOOK WITHOUT PLOT?<br /><br />Well, just take a look at the mess that is <i>Lola and the Boy Next Door</i>. <br /><br />Primarily, it was really just St. Clair’s situation told from a female teenager’s POV. Girl has boyfriend but falls in love with other guy – we’ve seen this before, have we not? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[We’ve even seen the ENDING before, have we not?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Secondly, there was no big climatic moment, not one that I could see. It was pretty much just a bunch of encounters between Lola and Cricket, lots of arguing in between, and a big dance. All obstacles Lola had to face were irrelevant, really, to the ending of the book. The missing continuity and urgency that would have existed had there been a plot present made this book so much weaker than it could have been.<br /><br /><b>Last but not Least: Special Guests Overstaying Their Welcome</b><br /> <br />It really saddens me to have to include this finale in this review, because Anna and St. Clair were really the reasons why I wanted to read this sequel. They had amazed me and blown me away (I’m a romantic, no matter how many people doubt that) and had left me wanting more. What SUCKS is that they were TOTALLY DIFFERENT PEOPLE!!! They told each other EVERY PART OF THEIR LIVES, they were together WAY TOO OFTEN, they had no lives outside of each other, and their dialogue was SO BLAND!! Like, COME ON!!! Not only that, but they were also WAYYYY too present. A simple peek-a-boo scene would have been fine, or like a run-into-them-at-the-mall would have been great, too. But no, they were present the entire time, they had purpose. Their presence in the story not only reminded me of how wonderful their book had been <s>and how much I wished I’d been reading it</s>, but it also gave all the other characters no space to breathe on their own. <br /><br />In short, I’ve overdosed on them. <br /><br /><b>Alas:</b><br /><br />I think I’m going to go take a nap, my friends. Like, I’m exhausted. I was so freaking excited to get this book, and then it had to just SUCK – no matter how much I really wanted to like it – and then I just had to write this review and get it all out there and dammit I wanna sleep.<br /><br />So. In conclusion, methinks I talked too much and I bet y’all are falling asleep at your desks right now, too, and so if there’s one thing to take away from this review, it’s this: <i>Anna and the French Kiss</i> was much, much better.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18299926722528557303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137096083?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Anna and the French Kiss</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Arlene by: </span>
      Etienne. I'm sticking to it... =)
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer137096083" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9632235584097174438"><i>First off, a huge thanks to <a href='http://www.rebeccabehrens.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rebecca</a> for giving me this ARC. Thank you!! </i><br/><br/>♥ ♥ ♥ <b>ABSOLUTELY CRUSH-WORTHY</b>♥ ♥ ♥<br/><br/>HOLY CRICKET!! I am absolutely in love with <b>Lola and the Boy Next Door</b>! I’m not denying it, I have a HUGE crush on this book and it’s not going away. Stephanie Perkins, without a doubt did it again. She’s managed to tap into my inner giddy making me a shameless book hugger. For fans of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss' title='Anna and the French Kiss by Stephanie Perkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Anna and the French Kiss</a> eagerly anticipating <b>Lola and the Boy Next Door</b> breathe with ease. This book is fr</span>
  <span id="freeText9632235584097174438" style="display:none"><i>First off, a huge thanks to <a href="http://www.rebeccabehrens.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Rebecca</a> for giving me this ARC. Thank you!! </i><br /><br />♥ ♥ ♥ <b>ABSOLUTELY CRUSH-WORTHY</b>♥ ♥ ♥<br /><br />HOLY CRICKET!! I am absolutely in love with <b>Lola and the Boy Next Door</b>! I’m not denying it, I have a HUGE crush on this book and it’s not going away. Stephanie Perkins, without a doubt did it again. She’s managed to tap into my inner giddy making me a shameless book hugger. For fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss" title="Anna and the French Kiss by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna and the French Kiss</a> eagerly anticipating <b>Lola and the Boy Next Door</b> breathe with ease. This book is fricken fabulous and just as loveable as her debut novel. PERFECTION! <br /><br />~ happy sigh~<br /><br />In this story, Lola, a budding designer with a quirky sense of style, has her world turned upside down when her old neighbors, the Bells, move back into their San Francisco Victorian home. It's been two years since she's seen the Bell twins; and her last encounter with Cricket was a hard lesson that crushes hurt like hell. Well this time around Lola is determined not to fall for him again. Why should she? She's older, more confident, has a sexy rocker boyfriend, it's all good... right? WRONG! <br /><br />Lola and Cricket had me smiling like an absolute dork the entire time. There is no way I could have read this book in public because I swear I was making some laugh-at-me faces. I just adore Perkins' style of delivering a slow building romance that blends perfectly with the flow of the entire story. As a reader, you can't help but fall into the storyline and ultimately resist the coming of the final chapters. It's the type of book you want to continue for endless chapters.<br /><br />There were parts of the story that reminded me of <i>Pretty in Pink</i> with Lola's quirky style and hand-made costumes. Cricket was pretty amazing too in the fashion department. These two make a perfect pair. Also, it was such a pleasure to have Anna and Etienne be a part of this novel. If you fell for Etienne in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss" title="Anna and the French Kiss by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna and the French Kiss</a>...watch out! You’ll swoon for him even harder in this book. <br /><br />As always, the writing is sharp, the characters are flawed to perfection, and the storyline is one that will have you smiling and sighing with love. <b>Lola and the Boy Next Door</b> has earned top ranking on my favorites list and I’m pretty sure it’s there to stay. ADORE!!!<br /><br />Realizing this isn’t a coherent review but rather a gush-fest about my book crush, I’ll stop now and just tell you that Perkins fans and YA Contemporary readers are going to enjoy this little gem to the tenth degree. <br /><br />P.S. Stephanie Perkins, I’ve been gushing about Aussie writers for the last few months and how they write the most amazing books. Well we’ve got you to brag about that’s just fine by me. XD Please don’t ever put your pen down or stop your mind from wandering into your happy place that holds your stories. It’s readers like me that adore what you put to paper. Beautiful stuff. Really!<br /><br /><b>Book quotes</b>: <br /><i>I know you aren't perfect. But it's a person's imperfections that make them perfect for someone else.<br /><br />Just because something isn't practical doesn't mean it's not worth creating. Sometimes beauty and real-life magic are enough.</i> <br /><br />These two book quotes are from an ARC, which will be compared and removed/updated based on the final copy, but I just had to include them... <br /><br />Okay, off it goes to the next Booker before Crystal pulls out her wand with her <i>ACCIO LOLA</i> magic. :D It’s coming twinie!! Enjoy!<br /></span>

    <a title="Jiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana"><img alt="Jiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540380229p2/10502567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1760790661?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jiana" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana">Jiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/30626646-lola-and-the-boy-next-door">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1760790661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4738155610836562450">No. NO. NO. JUST <b>NO</b>. This book is a mess. If you loved this book, then you might not want to read this review. Because I'm <i>so</i> annoyed right now. And my review will probably sound harsh to you. But I gotta let out all my anger.<br/><br/>Let me just start by saying that I loved Anna and the French Kiss. It was beyond enjoyable and adorable. But this? Oh my God. Lola and the Boy Next Door is a big fat <b>NO.</b> I'm beyond disappointed. <br/><br/>Cricket is a cutie. I liked Cricket. But, unfortunately, he was not enough to s</span>
  <span id="freeText4738155610836562450" style="display:none">No. NO. NO. JUST <b>NO</b>. This book is a mess. If you loved this book, then you might not want to read this review. Because I'm <i>so</i> annoyed right now. And my review will probably sound harsh to you. But I gotta let out all my anger.<br><br>Let me just start by saying that I loved Anna and the French Kiss. It was beyond enjoyable and adorable. But this? Oh my God. Lola and the Boy Next Door is a big fat <b>NO.</b> I'm beyond disappointed. <br><br>Cricket is a cutie. I liked Cricket. But, unfortunately, he was not enough to save this mess of a book. Cricket is the male lead, by the way. Not an insect. Can we talk about this name? What were you thinking, Stephanie? WHO NAMES THEIR CHARACTER AFTER AN INSECT, THAT LOOKS LIKE THIS? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483917596i/21661684._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, Anna and Etienne appear in this book, which was really nice because I love those two together.<br><br>Now, let's talk about the cause of all my problems with this book: LOLA. *yells and screams*<br><br>Okay.<br><br>Look.<br><br>I can't stand Lola. She's easily one of the my worst female heroines. I can't even begin to describe how much I couldn't stand her. Okay, so, Lola is supposedly 17 years old. She dresses up in wigs and <i>costumes</i> every single day. One day she wears a Swiss Heidi dress, the other she dresses up as Cleopatra, she went to FORMAL as Marie Antoinette etc. Basically her life is Halloween every day.<br><br><b><br>Who<br><br>the <br><br>hell<br><br>does<br><br>that?!<br></b><br><br>I know Perkins wanted to make Lola seem different and unique, but come <i>onnnn</i>, this is way too extreme. I get changing your styles every now and then, but dressing up in COSTUMES? Nope. That's just unrealistic to me and just ridiculous. Newsflash Lola, you're not 10 years old anymore, sweetie.<br><br><b>ALSO. Lola is beyond childish, dumb and selfish.</b> I know that at 17, nobody's beyond mature, but again, at 17, you're not beyond stupid either. Lola acts and talks and thinks like a 12 year old and I just could not handle her thoughts and her narration. Also, she's dating a 22 year old guy, Max, and then Cricket moves back to the neighborhood (he was her old crush) and the feelings are oh so back! YAAAY. No. <br><br>This is Lola during 90% of the book:<br>"I love Max."<br>"But Cricket is back."<br>"I am dating Max and he is the ONE!"<br>"Cricket is so tall and intelligent and amazing!"<br>"Max is my boyfriend and I am in love with him."<br>"But Cricket!!!!!"<br><br>Also, we are reminded every few pages how TALL Cricket is. Wow. <br><br>Max is described as an awesome boyfriend, but of course, for Lola to end up with Cricket, he has to do something bad for us to hate him, right? However, when they broke up, Max spoke truth. Harsh, yes. But the truth hurts sometimes.<br><br><b>I think that's enough roasting for Lola.</b><br><br>Now. The plot. Was there a plot though? There wasn't. The writing was all over the place in this book; however, in Anna and the French Kiss, it was way, way better. Again, this book is a mess.<br><br>I am so very disappointed and I hope Isla and the Happily Ever After is better. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4738155610836562450" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_600131880" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/600131880" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12842423-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539992905p2/12842423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/600131880?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/12842423-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142422014" href="/book/show/16101168-lola-and-the-boy-next-door">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer600131880" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8319664646398371599">I first read this book in May of 2013, and fell in love with Lola and Cricket's story. For some reason, I never wrote out a proper review for it though (although I do have reviews for Anna and the French Kiss and Isla and the Happily Ever After)<br/><br/>I just finished my first reread of the book, and it was the audiobook version. It was so good! I was so happy to be back with Lola and Cricket again! I love that this story is set in San Fransisco, and I just love all of the characters! <br/><br/>Lola reminds me of</span>
  <span id="freeText8319664646398371599" style="display:none">I first read this book in May of 2013, and fell in love with Lola and Cricket's story. For some reason, I never wrote out a proper review for it though (although I do have reviews for Anna and the French Kiss and Isla and the Happily Ever After)<br /><br />I just finished my first reread of the book, and it was the audiobook version. It was so good! I was so happy to be back with Lola and Cricket again! I love that this story is set in San Fransisco, and I just love all of the characters! <br /><br />Lola reminds me of Katy Perry, wearing these gorgeous costumes! I think she's such a fun character to read about! I love that she lives with her dads and her dog, Heavens to Betsy. I love that she's a vegetarian like me (that's just something that I dont' read about a lot so it really stands out to me!)I love that she basically only works at a movie theater (with Anna and St. Clare!!) just so she can afford all of her clothes and supplies she needs for her costumes. I think they are so special mainly because she makes them herself. I can't sew, so I always think it super cool when others like Lola can create entire outfits! Like how on earth can you do that?!<br /><br />I love that Cricket's sister figure skates, because I've always been interested in ice skating! Cricket... what a name.. what a guy. I love that he's an inventor. I can't say that I've read many books where the character makes another character mechanical parts for the skirt of a Marie Antoinette costume. <br /><br />I can't stand Max, and honestly I'm not sure that anyone likes him while reading this book. I think we all were happy to see that loser go.<br /><br />This is just such a sweet and fun story, and I highly recommend this to contemporary lovers! &lt;3<br />I wish Stephanie would write a whole series about these two.. I know we get to see them for a second in Isla and the Happily Ever After, but I'm anxious for more of their story!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8319664646398371599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7405902707697300356">D'AAWWWW, well isn't that just lovely.<br/><br/>Initial reactions:<br/>1. GAH, the cuteness OVERWHELMS ME! *faints*<br/>2. Okay. Serious business guys. Love the story. There are more things going on than just the boy next door. Family, figuring out who you really are, and growing up.<br/>3. Writing is amazing of course. Perkins is able to write her main characters with such a voice. They are complete characters. I love how Lola has interests, and there are issues surrounding her life other than boy problems. And althoug</span>
  <span id="freeText7405902707697300356" style="display:none">D'AAWWWW, well isn't that just lovely.<br /><br />Initial reactions:<br />1. GAH, the cuteness OVERWHELMS ME! *faints*<br />2. Okay. Serious business guys. Love the story. There are more things going on than just the boy next door. Family, figuring out who you really are, and growing up.<br />3. Writing is amazing of course. Perkins is able to write her main characters with such a voice. They are complete characters. I love how Lola has interests, and there are issues surrounding her life other than boy problems. And although she's her own character, you can't help but relate with her also.<br />4. Pacing is great! Lola's development as a character grew the more confused and distraught she got. She's learning and realizing what the right and hard things to do are.<br />5. OMG ANNA and ETIENNE. Oh how I missed you guys.<br />6. *GUSHES SOME MORE*<br />7. I love the setting of San Francisco. It has character, and a vibrancy about it that fits the characters.<br />8. It's really nice to read about the 'boy next door' character. They don't get enough attention, or usually pushed to the side by the mysterious, dark boy. Cricket, you are definitely my fav. boy next door. :)<br />9. *Tries to think of negatives.....* Can't be done.<br />10. Such a fun read. I wouldn't say it's light, because there are issues that I haven't really come across in books I've read before.<br /><br />You'll smile ear to ear after reading this book! I certainly did. Video review coming up soon.</span>

  <span id="freeText1795846675691271264" style="display:none">"And I hold my head high toward my big entrance, hand in hand with the boy who gave me the moon and the stars."<br /><br /><br />This is one of the sweetest books I've read. <br />Lola &amp; The Boy Next Door is a story about finding yourself in yourself, moving on, forgiviness, love and self-acceptance.<br />In the beggining I had a bit of a hard time. Getting Lola is quite a trip even though I liked her and I can say I'm glad I read this book. Phisycally I'm more like Anna but my personality is like Lola's and that made the reading so cool for me. <br />The characters were really well built (I love her parents relationship and how they raised her) and her best friend and Cricket. Oh, he's so sweet and I even liked that asshole (Max) as a character. So yeah, Stephanie really got me and I found myself laughing and hurting and that was a lot of fun.</span>

<div id="review_1411945568" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1411945568" />
    <a title="Amy | Foxy Blogs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs"><img alt="Amy | Foxy Blogs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366176904p2/9955253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1411945568?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy | Foxy Blogs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy | Foxy Blogs" href="/user/show/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs">Amy | Foxy Blogs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs?shelf=2015-books">2015-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs?shelf=library2go">library2go</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs?shelf=headphones">headphones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs?shelf=october-2015">october-2015</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1411945568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3839514082089601853"><b>FOUR POINT FIVE STARS</b><br/><br/>Two years ago I remember reading the first book in this series and enjoying it. So, when I was looking through the library's audios and saw this one I thought, <i>'why not.'</i><br/><br/>First off, I liked this one more than the first book. I know it's been two years since I read book one<b> but</b> this one was more fun to read. <br/><br/>What got my attention right away was <b>LOLA</b>. What an interesting character. She's a senior in high school who has a boyfriend who happens to be five years older than her. Ri</span>
  <span id="freeText3839514082089601853" style="display:none"><b>FOUR POINT FIVE STARS</b><br><br>Two years ago I remember reading the first book in this series and enjoying it. So, when I was looking through the library's audios and saw this one I thought, <i>'why not.'</i><br><br>First off, I liked this one more than the first book. I know it's been two years since I read book one<b> but</b> this one was more fun to read. <br><br>What got my attention right away was <b>LOLA</b>. What an interesting character. She's a senior in high school who has a boyfriend who happens to be five years older than her. Right there, I connected with her. While in high school I dated an older guy too (not quite as old as hers but to my parents too old for me). And now as a parent of teenagers myself I could connect with her parents. Now, I know why my parents thought it was a bad idea to date an older guy. <b>Hindsight is a wonderful thing.</b><br><br>I didn't realize this book was a love triangle until I got into the story. I'm not a fan of love triangles because someone always loses. I know there are a lot of 'Max haters' out there but I really felt for him. Of course, he's going to be jealous and suspicious when he feels Lola isn't be totally honest with him. Lola didn't do anything to make Max feel secure in their relationship. Here's another reason why her parents knew this relationship wasn't a good idea: a 17 year old and 22 year old are at two very different maturity levels and stages in their lives. He's a man and she's still a girl living under her parents rule. Too big of a difference. <br><br>Okay, enough about Lola and Max, and back to Lola. Lola is this girl whose parents are two dads. Her mom gave her up and her uncle and his partner adopted her. I loved how her dads parented her. <br><br>And of course this review wouldn't be complete with out mentioning the boy next door,<b> Cricket</b>. I loved this out-going guy. I can see why teen girls are swooning over him. <br><br>Overall, I really enjoyed this book. There's just something about young love that can be fun to read. What teens find to be "life ending" seems so trivial to us, who are adults, but I can remember being that age and have big ideals. <br><br>The narrator did a great job and if you like YA this would be a good option. <br><br><b>SERIES:</b><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss__Anna_and_the_French_Kiss___1_" title="Anna and the French Kiss (Anna and the French Kiss, #1) by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1358271931s/6936382.jpg" alt="Anna and the French Kiss (Anna and the French Kiss, #1) by Stephanie Perkins" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9961796.Lola_and_the_Boy_Next_Door__Anna_and_the_French_Kiss___2_" title="Lola and the Boy Next Door (Anna and the French Kiss, #2) by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1358271832s/9961796.jpg" alt="Lola and the Boy Next Door (Anna and the French Kiss, #2) by Stephanie Perkins" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9627755.Isla_and_the_Happily_Ever_After__Anna_and_the_French_Kiss___3_" title="Isla and the Happily Ever After (Anna and the French Kiss, #3) by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1362064564s/9627755.jpg" alt="Isla and the Happily Ever After (Anna and the French Kiss, #3) by Stephanie Perkins" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://foxyblogs.com" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_1656798904" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1656798904" />
    <a title="Nina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44463467-nina"><img alt="Nina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597502267p2/44463467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1656798904?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina" href="/user/show/44463467-nina">Nina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781409579946" href="/book/show/22247695-lola-and-the-boy-next-door">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44463467-nina?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1656798904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8330215015615949722"><i>“I know you aren't perfect. But it's a person's imperfections that make them perfect for someone else.” </i><br/><br/>I honestly don’t know why it took me so long to finally read “Lola and the Boy next Door”. I mean, I read “Anna and the French Kiss” five years ago and never even thought about continuing this series even though I loved the first book. <br/><br/>But now I finally read it and I’m so glad about that because LATBND was great. I almost loved it as much as I loved AATFK.<br/><br/>Just like the first book in the series</span>
  <span id="freeText8330215015615949722" style="display:none"><i>“I know you aren't perfect. But it's a person's imperfections that make them perfect for someone else.” </i><br /><br />I honestly don’t know why it took me so long to finally read “Lola and the Boy next Door”. I mean, I read “Anna and the French Kiss” five years ago and never even thought about continuing this series even though I loved the first book. <br /><br />But now I finally read it and I’m so glad about that because LATBND was great. I almost loved it as much as I loved AATFK.<br /><br />Just like the first book in the series, this is a very quick and cute read. You can easily read this book in one sitting; by now I’m even starting to believe you could read the entire series in one sitting though I won’t know about that for sure until I’ve also read “Isla and the Happily Ever After”. <br /><br />The basics of the plot of this book are very similar to the plot of AATFK. Once again, we have two teenagers. One of them is in a relationship and the other isn’t but they start feeling drawn to each other though they don’t want to admit it because they’re actually just friends. Some other things happen and you have a lot of stuff you can laugh about. That means that this book once again isn’t anything new and unique; but it’s another one of those books that just make you incredibly happy and will make you feel good about life which makes it perfect. <br /><br />Since it is the sequel to AATFK, we also get to read about Anna and St. Clair again which already made me fall in love with this book before I had even really gotten into it. I think even if LATBND had been horrible, I would’ve still decided to reread it at some point just because of my two favorites. <br /><br />But there is one thing that bugged me about this book and that resulted in me not liking it as much as I liked AATFK. My problem is that I think that Lola is a bit of an annoying character. During the first half of the book I was still able to mostly ignore but it got worse during the second half of the book. There were moments during which she was acting quite immature even though she was constantly trying to act older than she actually was. I also thought that the fact that she was always wearing costumes with wigs and all that stuff was a little too much. Maybe I am just too old for a character like that or I didn’t like it because I think it’s extremely weird to always run around in colorful costumes with often colorful wigs on your head even when you’re just going to school. I know that it is everyone’s own decision and it made her kind of unique, but it just didn’t help in that situation. Seeing her act so immature at some point and then imagining her with blue hair in a dress she made out of a picnic blanket was just a little too much for me. <br /><br />That’s why I decided to give LATBND only 4 out of 5 stars. All in all though, it was a great book that is just as addictive as AATFK. It’s an adorable love story and I’ll definitely reread it one day even though I don’t like Lola that much. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8330215015615949722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7385574146302076611">3.5 stars<br/><br/>This book is exactly how I expected it to be. Light, meh main character, and predictable. The main thing I love about this is Stephanie Perkins is just a great writer. She writes contemporary romances so well and I really find it enjoyable to read. I knew going into this that the main thing I wouldn't get along with is Lola.   <span id="freeText7385574146302076611" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />This book is exactly how I expected it to be. Light, meh main character, and predictable. The main thing I love about this is Stephanie Perkins is just a great writer. She writes contemporary romances so well and I really find it enjoyable to read. I knew going into this that the main thing I wouldn't get along with is Lola. I've heard things about Lola, and kinda had a preconceived notion of her, and my prediction that I wouldn't like her was correct. She just seemed.... ingenuine to me. Too quirky, to the point where I couldn't relate to her and it felt like everything she did was a childish cry for attention. On the other hand, I loved every other character in this book. Her gay parents and Cricket, especially. I didn't like how a lot of this book was Lola refusing to break up with her boyfriend, and the entire love triangle (????) was really underwhelming because you know she's gonna end up with Cricket. I mean, the book is titled lola and the boy next door. the entire book is based around them. So nothing in this book surprised me, and it followed a really typical pace of a stephanie perkins (or, any YA) romance. But it was pretty cute, even though a lot of it was predictable and cheesy and typical for YA cutesie books. It was a nice surprise to see Etienne and Anna so present in this one; I had thought maybe they'd just appear once or twice but they really made me happy seeing their storyline :D<br /><br />I'm picking up Isla next and i'm already enjoying chapter one so here's to finishing this series finally!</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_145820832" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145820832" />
    <a title="Lucy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3813315-lucy"><img alt="Lucy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307662921p2/3813315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145820832?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy" href="/user/show/3813315-lucy">Lucy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=make-room-for-that-sequel">make-room-for-that-sequel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=story-what-story">story-what-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=i-feel-bad-for-not-liking-it">i-feel-bad-for-not-liking-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145820832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4727186650505683625"><i>Lola and the Boy Next Door</i> was a clumsy fumble for Stephanie Perkins. It had the potential to be something much better, but got bogged down with Anna's history and Isla's future. I often wondered how much of Lola was planned while <i>Anna and the French Kiss</i> was being written and how much of Lola's story was simply dictated by the circumstances the first story had and the third story would require. Even Perkins' charming writing couldn't really save the book after tying it to so many heavy bricks a</span>
  <span id="freeText4727186650505683625" style="display:none"><i>Lola and the Boy Next Door</i> was a clumsy fumble for Stephanie Perkins. It had the potential to be something much better, but got bogged down with Anna's history and Isla's future. I often wondered how much of Lola was planned while <i>Anna and the French Kiss</i> was being written and how much of Lola's story was simply dictated by the circumstances the first story had and the third story would require. Even Perkins' charming writing couldn't really save the book after tying it to so many heavy bricks and tossing it in the ocean to see if it would float.<br /><br />Cricket, the male romantic lead, is the boy next door from the title, but he wasn't involved in the story enough. The story was more like <i>Lola and Her Two Dads,</i> <i>Lola and Her Crazy Wigs,</i> <i>Lola and The Drug Addict Birth Mother,</i> <i>Lola and The Slightly Pedophilic Rock Star Boyfriend.</i> Lola and Cricket? Not so much. Cricket is part of the story, but he isn't the central figure Etienne was for Anna. The fact that so much of their romance is told instead of shown didn't help with developing or moving him into the spot light. Their history which was supposed to be a Very Big Deal was told in a chapter and it was Not a Very Big Deal, which made Lola seem petty and self-centered rather than sympathetic and someone easy to like.<br /><br />And because you want to know what the (Not) Very Big Deal was:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The romance that began to bloom between Lola and Cricket got squished by a couple of misunderstandings and some unkind manipulation from Cricket's sister, Calliope. Lola thought Cricket lied to her about his birthday party and deliberately didn't invite her; she thought this because his sister yelled at her for not coming and looked all shocked when Lola told her she wasn't invited. Cricket thought Lola didn't come to his birthday because Callope said she'd invited Lola. Big fucking deal. Cricket moved away before they could work out this little half hour sitcom. If Lola had moved beyond the incident a little instead of having a panic attack and dropping plates when he moved back in then I wouldn't be annoyed the event was so trivial. Advice to authors: don't build it up like he ran over her dog, kissed her best friend, and read her diary over the school speaker system all in the same day when it's really a 24 minute sitcom misunderstanding. You will just piss me off. Live up to what you're trying to sell, please. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />For the first 30% of the book Cricket's presence is mostly inconsequential. At one point I wrote 'blah' as a status update because nothing was actually happening between them. The pieces were on the board, the back story was set up, and then nothing was put into motion because the author kept getting distracted by Anna and Etienne and their l-o-v-e. Yes, I loved Anna and Etienne. Putting so much of them in right at the start, however, was both detrimental to Lola's story and reminded me of a more compelling and interesting story I'd rather be re-reading...<br /><br />Anyway, Lola's boyfriend, Max, starts out okay, but as Cricket creeps his gangly legs further into the book Max starts acting more like a dick? He goes from being the guy who deals with all of her parents rules for her, including awkward interrogation style brunches once a week to some weird half-a-pedo who calls her his Lolita. (He's 22 and she's 17.) I wasn't crazy about the age difference, but it was being dealt with in a reasonable way by her parents. I can deal with slightly icky age differences if they're acknowledged and dealt with in the story and/or fit with the world building. Still I got wrinkled nose when he started calling her Lolita, which was exactly the reaction I was supposed to have. We were supposed to be okay with Max until we weren't supposed to be okay with Max. It was all very choreographed and forced.<br /><br />I know there's no way to please the audience completely on the Max front. There are people who will say Lola should have just dropped him because she was more attracted to Cricket -- that the demonizing him was just for author convenience. Then there will be people who would have disliked Lola for just dropping her boyfriend because she feels an old flame for someone else blah blah blah. My opinion is that making Max the bad guy to wash Lola's hands was cheap. I can only say how I would've wanted to be treated in Max's position. If someone I was dating wanted to be with someone else I'd want them to go. I've been in that place once -- the one where you're standing in front of someone and they're looking over your shoulder at someone else. Being a place holder sucks. You're not doing me any big favor wasting my time if there's somewhere else you'd rather be.<br /><br />After the inevitable break up with Lola and Max, she takes months to figure out how to be with Cricket. It involves a lot of black clothes and the reader being told they hang out sometimes, with only brief snapshots of it. At random points the jump point for Isla is set up, with Cricket's sister possibly competing in France and Anna and Etienne (who are somehow suddenly mysteriously not broke now?) both wanting to go back to Paris for a visit (even though they were there six months ago).<br /><br />There are some swoon-worthy scenes. Cricket climbing through the window that second time and asking if she still loved Max? Loved it. Didn't save the book for me though. There were too many awkward things weighing it down before and after. Like, Cricket doing her hair? Weird to me because at Calliope's competition level her fluffy haired brother wouldn't be fixing her hair and also the fact that Lola's own hair was such a constant rat nest under her wigs totally skeeved me. Also, the story about the boy with the stars and the moon? Could've bought it if we knew the stars on his hand meant Lola earlier in the book. Instead it was AWKWARDLY worked in right before he gave her the mechanical star and moon gift which lessened the effect. <br /><br />I couldn't give this book the five stars I was expecting to give it when I pre-ordered. I can't even pre-order the next book because I'm not sure I want to read anymore tie-in books. I might have to wait for Perkins to start doing independent, unrelated stories before I can claim fan status again. I can't even give four stars because it's not an exceptional book. It's ho-hum. Good but not great, not something I'd run out to buy again. Blah.<br /><br />I will say this, I loved her dads. I think I could've liked Cricket's sister and Lola's best friend Lindsey if they'd been allowed to develop, but these aspects of the story are part of what was shrunk down by Anna's history and Isla's set up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4727186650505683625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1589335399" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1589335399" />
    <a title="Jenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14772037-jenna"><img alt="Jenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544410363p2/14772037.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1589335399?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna" href="/user/show/14772037-jenna">Jenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone looking for a fun read!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=contemporary-reads">contemporary-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=romance-reads">romance-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=4-star-books">4-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=fall-2016-tbr">fall-2016-tbr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1589335399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2648035050004431127"><b>A bowl full of fun!</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467210472ra/19565422.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><p>Stephanie Perkins has not disappointed me yet! Lola and The Boy Next door is about 17 year old Lola (or Dolores, if she's in trouble). She has an older boyfriend, strict parents and a great best friend. Her boyfriend Max is 22, in a band and totally cool. Her dads are strict, but caring and other than their strict dating rules, Lola doesn't mind. Lindsay is her best friend and can sense when something is up or guess how Lola is feeling almost immediately. Lola thinks she's hap</p></span>
  <span id="freeText2648035050004431127" style="display:none"><b>A bowl full of fun!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467210472ra/19565422.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><p>Stephanie Perkins has not disappointed me yet! Lola and The Boy Next door is about 17 year old Lola (or Dolores, if she's in trouble). She has an older boyfriend, strict parents and a great best friend. Her boyfriend Max is 22, in a band and totally cool. Her dads are strict, but caring and other than their strict dating rules, Lola doesn't mind. Lindsay is her best friend and can sense when something is up or guess how Lola is feeling almost immediately. Lola thinks she's happy with her life until her neighbours move back in. Her neighbours left 2 years prior and they did not leave on good terms. Their return brings anxiety, curiosity, trouble and lot's of confusing feelings for Lola. I consider this book a contemporary but also a romance since the main plot line is about Lola's relationships. </p><br><p> The writing in this book makes for a quirky, fun-loving read. It shouldn't take you long to read and you'll get right into the story. I love Stephanie Perkins writing style and can't wait to read even more of her books!</p><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477614116ra/20971763.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>One of my favourite parts about this series is the quirky but relatable traits/thought processes of the characters! For example; this is an excerpt from Lola and The Boy Next Door that I found particularly funny:<br><b> "I wonder if he's looking at my butt. WHY DID I JUST THINK THAT? Now my butt feels COLOSSAL. Maybe he's looking at my legs. Is that better? Or worse? Do I want him looking at me? I hold on to the bottom of my dress as I climb into the backseat and crawl to the other side. I'm sure he's looking at my butt. He has to be. It's huge, and it's right there, and it's huge. No. I'm acting crazy." </b><br>It's parts like this that get me laughing and feel connected to the character. Even if you can't relate, it's nice to be able to see their thought processes and you get the chance to understand the character.<br><p> I gave this book 4/5 stars because I genuinally enjoyed it and would recommend. It didn't get 5 stars due to a certain plot line <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ How it was evident that Lola liked Cricket and that she knew she liked Cricket but continued to lie to Max. Especially when Max would straight up ask her, he wasn't clueless and then she'd lie. She then continued to lead on Cricket, even after Calliope gave her SUCH A GOOD reality check.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and how it dragged on for most of the book. They could have been wrapped up faster but to drag it on that long made me extremely frustrated with Lola's decisions. Another reason I only gave it 4/5 stars is because certain plot lines were never finished. I didn't get closure with them or find out what happens! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I'm talking about if Calliope eventually broke her curse or how she did at the olympics. Did Lola go to the olympics with St. Clair, Anna and Cricket? Did Lindsay ever decide that her and Charlie should date for real? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382227545ra/5761185.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Overall I really liked this book and would recommend it if anyone needs a fun book to read! It's really refreshing to read after a depressing book or high fantasy book. <br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br>Quick, expressive and smooth writing means another one of Stephanie Perkins books! This book isn't 5 stars for me due to the plot mostly. It was extremely predictable, but not only that, the MC was in a relationship with someone while she lead on and pursued another guy. I wasn't a huge fan of that, especially for how long it dragged out for. Anyways I will publish a full review this evening!! This is just a quick summary of what I thought!</p></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2648035050004431127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RENIfw5Ol0Yvp4i31QbJcoHGU3UFYfY8JuTNQb6/a1MR1lKs/oFdObC4d01xjXgAXxIuTpdwYjRxsmj82qG3sg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cUJQ1aJnp1I1qlSQrBDbpIkS7gpk+rLFBgVGFdmqn5ck10oGUqhtLaq1q2oIm2rWV8aTMfbrJs1RU+OovbRDdg==')})
  }

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/7149084-lola-and-the-boy-next-door">Quotes from Lola and the Boy ...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I know you aren't perfect. But it's a person's imperfections that make them perfect for someone else.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/398118-i-know-you-aren-t-perfect-but-it-s-a-person-s-imperfections">1888 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Once upon a time, there was a girl who talked to the moon. And she was mysterious and she was perfect, in that way that girls who talk to moons are. In the house next door, there lived a boy. And the boy watched the girl grow more and more perfect, more and more beautiful with each passing year. He watched her watch the moon. And he began to wonder if the moon would help him unravel the mystery of the beautiful girl. So the boy looked into the sky. But he couldn't concentrate on the moon. He was too distracted by the stars. And it didn't matter how many songs or poems had already been written about them, because whenever he thought about the girl, the stars shone brighter. As if she were the one keeping them illuminated. <br /><br />One day, the boy had to move away. He couldn't bring the girl with him, so he brought the stars. When he'd look out his window at night, he would start with one. One star. And the boy would make a wish on it, and the wish would be her name.<br /><br />At the sound of her name, a second star would appear. And then he'd wish her name again, and the stars would double into four. And four became eight, and eight became sixteen, and so on, in the greatest mathematical equation the universe had ever seen. And by the time an hour had passed, the sky would be filled with so many stars that it would wake the neighbors. People wondered who'd turned on the floodlights.<br /><br />The boy did. By thinking about the girl.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/442361-once-upon-a-time-there-was-a-girl-who-talked">1277 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
